---

## QUICK START: FIRST-TIME USER WORKFLOW

```
1. Pick a simple concept (10s, one shot, no dialogue)
2. Use a prompt template from SORA2_READY_TO_USE_TEMPLATES
3. Generate 3 versions
4. Pick the best one
5. Export and share
6. Document what worked

Don't overthink your first project. The goal is to learn the system.
```

---

*Version 2.0 | December 2025*  
*Use with SORA 2 EXPERT PROFILE, PROMPT BUILDER, and TROUBLESHOOTING FLOWCHART*


## File: SORA2_Documentation/SORA2_PROMPT_BUILDER.md

# SORA 2 INTERACTIVE PROMPT BUILDER

**Version:** 2.0  
**Purpose:** Step-by-step prompt construction tool  
**Time to Complete:** 5-10 minutes per prompt

---

## HOW TO USE THIS BUILDER

1. Work through each section sequentially
2. Fill in only what's relevant to your shot
3. Copy the final assembled prompt
4. Iterate based on results

---

## SECTION 1: PROJECT SETUP

### Quick Info
```
[ ] Shot Duration: _____ seconds (4, 8, 10, 15, 20, 25)
[ ] Aspect Ratio: _____ (16:9 landscape, 9:16 portrait, 1:1 square)
[ ] Quality Tier: _____ (Standard, Pro)
[ ] Project Name: _____________________
[ ] Shot Number: _____________________
```

### Creative Brief (Optional but Recommended)
```
What's the purpose of this shot?
_________________________________________________

What emotion should it evoke?
_________________________________________________

Platform destination? (YouTube, TikTok, Instagram, etc.)
_________________________________________________
```

---

## SECTION 2: STYLE SPINE
*This anchors your entire aesthetic - everything else builds on this*

### Choose ONE Primary Style:
```
[ ] Photorealistic Cinema
[ ] Analog/VHS Vintage
[ ] Documentary Handheld
[ ] Commercial Clean
[ ] Anime/Animation
[ ] Horror/Dark
[ ] Sci-Fi Futuristic
[ ] Other: _________________
```

### Realism Anchor (for photorealistic):
```
[ ] Shot on ARRI Alexa 65, 4K DCI
[ ] Shot on RED V-RAPTOR 8K
[ ] Shot on Sony VENICE 2
[ ] _DSC09421.ARW (Sony sensor emulation)
[ ] Canon EOS C500 Mark II
[ ] Photorealistic, 8K resolution
[ ] Custom: _________________
```

### Era/Aesthetic (if applicable):
```
[ ] Modern/Contemporary (2020s)
[ ] 2010s Digital
[ ] 2000s Early Digital
[ ] 1990s DV/Grunge
[ ] 1980s VHS/Neon
[ ] 1970s Film Grain/Warm
[ ] 1960s Technicolor
[ ] 1950s Mid-Century
[ ] Custom: _________________
```

---

## SECTION 3: SUBJECT & ACTION

### Primary Subject:
```
WHO/WHAT is the focus?
_________________________________________________
_________________________________________________

Physical description (age, features, wardrobe):
_________________________________________________
_________________________________________________
```

### Action Breakdown (Use Beatmap Format):
```
H0.00 | Opening frame/position:
_________________________________________________

B2.00 | First action (what changes):
_________________________________________________

B4.00 | Second action (development):
_________________________________________________

B6.00 | Third action (escalation):
_________________________________________________

P8.00 | Peak moment:
_________________________________________________

E10.00 | Final hold/resolution:
_________________________________________________
```

### Secondary Elements (if any):
```
Background characters/objects:
_________________________________________________

Props in scene:
_________________________________________________
```

---

## SECTION 4: ENVIRONMENT

### Location:
```
WHERE is this happening?
_________________________________________________

Specific details (e.g., "abandoned broadcast studio circa 1987"):
_________________________________________________
_________________________________________________
```

### Time of Day:
```
[ ] Golden hour (sunrise/sunset)
[ ] Blue hour (twilight)
[ ] Midday (harsh sun)
[ ] Overcast/Cloudy
[ ] Night
[ ] Interior (specify lighting)
[ ] Custom: _________________
```

### Atmosphere:
```
[ ] Clear
[ ] Fog/Mist (density: light / medium / heavy)
[ ] Rain (intensity: drizzle / steady / downpour)
[ ] Snow
[ ] Dust particles in light
[ ] Smoke/Haze
[ ] Custom: _________________
```

---

## SECTION 5: CAMERA SYSTEM

### Shot Type:
```
[ ] Extreme Wide (XWS) - Vast landscape
[ ] Wide (WS) - Full environment + subject
[ ] Full Shot (FS) - Head to toe
[ ] Medium Wide (MWS) - Knees up
[ ] Medium (MS) - Waist up
[ ] Medium Close-up (MCU) - Chest up
[ ] Close-up (CU) - Face fills frame
[ ] Extreme Close-up (XCU) - Eyes, lips, hands
[ ] POV - Character's viewpoint
[ ] Over-the-shoulder (OTS)
[ ] Custom: _________________
```

### Camera Angle:
```
[ ] Eye level - Neutral
[ ] Low angle - Looking up (power)
[ ] High angle - Looking down (vulnerability)
[ ] Dutch/Canted - Tilted (unease)
[ ] Bird's eye - Overhead
[ ] Worm's eye - Ground level up
```

### Lens Focal Length:
```
[ ] 14-24mm - Ultra wide, environmental
[ ] 24-35mm - Natural wide
[ ] 35-50mm - Standard, human eye
[ ] 50-85mm - Portrait compression
[ ] 85-135mm - Telephoto intimacy
[ ] 135mm+ - Extreme compression
[ ] Custom: _____mm
```

### Aperture (Depth of Field):
```
[ ] f/1.4-2.0 - Extreme shallow DOF, dreamy
[ ] f/2.8-4.0 - Subject isolation with context
[ ] f/5.6-8.0 - Balanced sharpness
[ ] f/11-16 - Deep focus, everything sharp
```

### Camera Movement (PICK ONLY ONE):
```
[ ] Static - Locked tripod, no movement
[ ] Dolly-in - Push toward subject
[ ] Dolly-out - Pull away from subject
[ ] Truck left/right - Lateral slide
[ ] Crane up/down - Vertical arc
[ ] Pan left/right - Horizontal rotation
[ ] Tilt up/down - Vertical rotation
[ ] Handheld - Human shake (specify intensity: subtle / medium / heavy)
[ ] Steadicam - Smooth following
[ ] Arc - Semicircular path around subject
[ ] Custom: _________________

Movement speed:
[ ] Static (0 ft/sec)
[ ] Subtle drift (0.1-0.3 ft/sec)
[ ] Slow dolly (0.5-1.0 ft/sec)
[ ] Walk pace (2-3 ft/sec)
[ ] Fast track (4-6 ft/sec)
```

---

## SECTION 6: LIGHTING DESIGN

### Key Light (Primary):
```
Source type:
[ ] Natural sunlight
[ ] Window light
[ ] Tungsten (3200K warm)
[ ] Daylight balanced (5600K)
[ ] Fluorescent (green cast)
[ ] LED RGB
[ ] Practical (in-scene lamp/fixture)
[ ] Custom: _________________

Direction:
[ ] Camera left
[ ] Camera right
[ ] Overhead
[ ] Below (underlighting)
[ ] Backlight/Rim
[ ] Front/Key
```

### Fill Light (Secondary):
```
[ ] None (high contrast)
[ ] Soft fill (reduces shadows)
[ ] Bounce light (natural wrap)
[ ] Ambient (environmental)
```

### Contrast Ratio:
```
[ ] 2:1 - Flat, broadcast
[ ] 4:1 - Natural, balanced
[ ] 8:1 - Dramatic, cinematic
[ ] 12:1 - High contrast, thriller
[ ] 20:1+ - Noir, extreme
```

---

```
Color 1: _________________ (applied to: ________________)
Color 2: _________________ (applied to: ________________)
Color 3: _________________ (applied to: ________________)
```

### Color Temperature:
```
[ ] Warm (orange, amber, golden)
[ ] Neutral (balanced)
[ ] Cool (blue, teal, cyan)
[ ] Mixed (warm key, cool fill)
```

### Grade/Look Reference:
```
[ ] Teal and orange (Hollywood blockbuster)
[ ] Bleach bypass (desaturated, contrasty)
[ ] Film print emulation (crushed blacks)
[ ] Day for night (blue, underexposed)
[ ] Kodak Vision3 500T (warm tungsten)
[ ] Fujifilm Eterna (muted Japanese)
[ ] Custom: _________________
```

```
_________________________________________________

_________________________________________________
```

### Atmospheric Particles:

```

Character speaks: "_____________________________________"

```

### Ambient Sound Bed:
```
Primary ambient:
_________________________________________________

_________________________________________________
```

### Sound Effects (Key Moments):
```
At ___s: _________________________________________
At ___s: _________________________________________
At ___s: _________________________________________
```

### Music (if applicable):
```
[ ] None
[ ] Subtle ambient bed
[ ] Synth pulse (specify BPM: ____)
[ ] Custom: _________________
```

---

## SECTION 10: NEGATIVE CONSTRAINTS

### Things to EXPLICITLY AVOID:
```
[ ] Morphing/shape changes
[ ] Teleporting objects
[ ] Floating/weightless physics
[ ] Text/logos/signage
[ ] Lens flares (unless specified)
[ ] Inconsistent lighting
[ ] Extra limbs/fingers
[ ] AI aesthetic/plastic skin
[ ] Digital noise/artifacts
[ ] Custom: _________________
```

---

## SECTION 11: PHYSICS & REALISM (If Applicable)

### Material Properties:
```
Weight/Mass:
[ ] Light (paper, feather, balloon)
[ ] Medium (book, phone, cup)
[ ] Heavy (bowling ball, anvil, car door)

Friction:
[ ] Low (ice, polished marble, wet tile)
[ ] Medium (wood, concrete, grass)
[ ] High (rubber, sandpaper, carpet)

Elasticity:
[ ] High (rubber ball)
[ ] Medium (basketball)
[ ] Low (tennis ball)
[ ] None (sandbag, clay)
```

### Forces to Specify:
```
[ ] Realistic gravity/acceleration
[ ] Momentum/inertia effects
[ ] Wind (specify speed: ____ km/h)
[ ] Water/fluid dynamics
[ ] Impact/collision forces
```

---

## FINAL ASSEMBLY

### Copy & Paste Your Prompt:

```
[STYLE SPINE]
Shot on [camera body], [resolution], [era aesthetic if applicable].

[SUBJECT & ACTION]
[Subject description] in [environment].
At [time]s, [first action].
At [time]s, [second action].
At [time]s, [peak moment].
[Final hold description].

[CAMERA]
[Shot type], [focal length], [aperture].
Camera movement: [movement type at speed].
[Angle specification].

[LIGHTING]
[Key light source] from [direction], [contrast ratio].
[Fill/secondary lighting].

[COLOR]
Palette: [color 1], [color 2], [color 3].
Grade: [look reference].

[TEXTURE]
[Grain percentage], [material details], [atmospheric particles].

[AUDIO]
Dialogue: "[line]" ([delivery note])
Ambient: [sound bed description]
SFX: [key sound effects with timing]
[Music if any]

Duration: [X seconds]

AVOID: [negative constraints list]
```

---

## QUICK CHECKLIST BEFORE GENERATION

```
[ ] Subject clearly described with distinguishing features
[ ] Action broken into timed beats (2-3 second intervals)
[ ] Environment/location specified with era if relevant
[ ] Camera specs complete (shot type, lens, movement)
[ ] Lighting direction and sources defined
[ ] Color palette chosen (2-3 colors)
[ ] Audio elements specified (even if just ambient)
[ ] Negative constraints included
[ ] Duration matches complexity (shorter = higher quality)
[ ] All technical terms spelled correctly
```

---

## ITERATION NOTES

After generating, record what worked/didn't work:

**Generation 1:**
```
What worked: _____________________________________________
What didn't: _____________________________________________
Adjustment for next try: __________________________________
```

**Generation 2:**
```
What worked: _____________________________________________
What didn't: _____________________________________________
Final adjustment: _________________________________________
```

---

## ADVANCED: MULTI-SHOT SEQUENCES

If creating multiple shots for a sequence:

### Continuity Anchors (REPEAT IN EVERY SHOT):
```
Character description: ____________________________________
Wardrobe: ________________________________________________
Lighting direction: _______________________________________
Color grade: _____________________________________________
Time of day: _____________________________________________
```

### Shot Progression:
```
SHOT 1 (0-[X]s): [Wide establishing]
[Full prompt]

SHOT 2 ([X]-[Y]s): [Medium coverage]
[Full prompt with continuity anchors]

SHOT 3 ([Y]-[Z]s): [Close-up payoff]
[Full prompt with continuity anchors]
```

## File: SORA2_Documentation/SORA2_TROUBLESHOOTING_FLOWCHART.md

# SORA 2 TROUBLESHOOTING FLOWCHART & DIAGNOSTIC GUIDE

**Version:** 2.0  
**Purpose:** Quick problem identification and fixes  
**Avg Resolution Time:** 5-15 minutes

---

## HOW TO USE THIS GUIDE

1. Identify your problem category
2. Follow the diagnostic path
3. Apply fixes in order (easiest to most complex)
4. Test after each fix
5. Document what worked for future reference

---

## PROBLEM CATEGORY INDEX

1. [Visual Quality Issues](#1-visual-quality-issues)
2. [Motion & Physics Problems](#2-motion--physics-problems)
3. [Character Consistency Failures](#3-character-consistency-failures)
4. [Audio Sync Issues](#4-audio-sync-issues)
5. [Camera Movement Problems](#5-camera-movement-problems)
6. [Lighting Inconsistencies](#6-lighting-inconsistencies)
7. [Style/Aesthetic Drift](#7-styleaesthetic-drift)
8. [Text/Logo Artifacts](#8-textlogo-artifacts)
9. [Generation Speed/Quality Trade-offs](#9-generation-speedquality-trade-offs)
10. [Multi-Shot Continuity Breaks](#10-multi-shot-continuity-breaks)

---

## 1. VISUAL QUALITY ISSUES

### SYMPTOM: Blurry, pixelated, or soft focus output

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: Is the blur uniform across the frame or selective?
├─ Uniform blur → Resolution/quality issue
│   FIX 1: Switch to higher resolution (Pro tier)
│   FIX 2: Reduce duration (10s → 8s → 4s)
│   FIX 3: Add "sharp focus, 8K detail" to prompt
│   FIX 4: Remove any references to "cinematic bokeh" if not intended
│
└─ Selective blur → Depth of field issue
    FIX 1: Specify aperture: "f/5.6, balanced focus"
    FIX 2: State what should be sharp: "sharp focus on subject's face"
    FIX 3: Add "deep focus" if everything should be sharp
```

**PROMPT ADDITIONS TO TRY:**
```
"Crisp detail, sharp focus throughout frame, 8K resolution"
"High clarity, no motion blur, precise textures"
```

**AVOID IN PROMPT:**
```
"Dreamy," "soft," "ethereal," "hazy" (unless intentional)
```

---

### SYMPTOM: Digital artifacts, banding, compression

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: When do artifacts appear?
├─ Throughout video → Generation issue
│   FIX 1: Add to negatives: "no compression artifacts, no banding, no digital noise"
│   FIX 2: Specify "film grain" instead of letting digital noise appear
│   FIX 3: Reduce scene complexity (fewer elements)
│   FIX 4: Try during off-peak hours
│
└─ In specific areas (gradients, dark regions) → Technical limitation
    FIX 1: Avoid smooth gradients (sunsets, fog) in favor of textured alternatives
    FIX 2: Add texture overlays in post
    FIX 3: Work with current output, enhance in post-production
```

**PREVENTION:**
```
- Include "no banding, clean gradients" in negatives
- Specify "organic film grain" for texture
- Avoid prompting for "smooth gradients" or "perfect skies"
```

---

### SYMPTOM: Oversaturated or undersaturated colors

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: Is saturation consistent or shifting?
├─ Consistently off → Style token issue
│   FIX 1: Specify saturation level: "natural color saturation"
│   FIX 2: Add color grade reference: "Kodak Vision3 balanced color"
│   FIX 3: For less saturation: "muted palette, desaturated"
│   FIX 4: For more saturation: "vibrant color, rich saturation"
│
└─ Shifting during video → Lighting/exposure drift
    FIX 1: Lock exposure: "consistent exposure throughout"
    FIX 2: Specify lighting consistency: "even lighting, no exposure shifts"
    FIX 3: Shorten duration for better consistency
```

**SATURATION KEYWORDS:**
```
INCREASE: vibrant, saturated, rich color, Technicolor, vivid
DECREASE: muted, desaturated, washed out, faded, matte
NEUTRAL: natural color, balanced saturation, realistic tones
```

---

## 2. MOTION & PHYSICS PROBLEMS

### SYMPTOM: Objects floating, defying gravity, weightless

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: What type of object is floating?
├─ Heavy objects (furniture, people, vehicles) → Physics description missing
│   FIX 1: Add weight specification: "heavy wooden table, realistic gravity"
│   FIX 2: Describe settling: "falls with realistic acceleration, settles naturally"
│   FIX 3: Include ground contact: "feet firmly planted on floor"
│   FIX 4: Add to negatives: "no floating, no weightless motion"
│
├─ Light objects (papers, fabric) → Force description needed
│   FIX 1: Describe forces: "paper flutters naturally in 5 mph breeze"
│   FIX 2: Specify material: "lightweight cotton fabric, realistic drape"
│
└─ Liquids/fluids → Physics parameters missing
    FIX 1: Describe viscosity: "water pours with natural viscosity"
    FIX 2: Add splash dynamics: "creates realistic splash on impact"
    FIX 3: Specify settling: "ripples spread naturally and fade"
```

**PHYSICS KEYWORDS TO ADD:**
```
"Realistic gravity and momentum"
"Natural weight distribution"
"Objects obey physics laws"
"Authentic material properties"
```

**AVOID:**
```
Removing these or contradictory terms like "floats gently" for non-buoyant objects
```

---

### SYMPTOM: Morphing, melting, shape-shifting objects

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: What's morphing?
├─ Subject's body/face → Character description insufficient
│   FIX 1: Lock anatomy: "maintains consistent human anatomy throughout"
│   FIX 2: Add structural details: "rigid bone structure, no facial distortion"
│   FIX 3: Reduce duration (8s → 4s)
│   FIX 4: Simplify action (less extreme movement)
│
├─ Objects → Material rigidity not specified
│   FIX 1: Specify material: "rigid carbon fiber, maintains shape"
│   FIX 2: Lock form: "solid structure, no warping or melting"
│   FIX 3: Add to negatives: "no morphing, no shape changes, no melting"
│
└─ Background elements → Scene complexity too high
    FIX 1: Simplify background: fewer elements
    FIX 2: Lock environment: "static background, consistent architecture"
    FIX 3: Reduce video duration
```

**PROMPT ADDITIONS:**
```
"Maintains consistent form throughout"
"Solid structure, no warping"
"Anatomically correct, no distortion"
```

---

### SYMPTOM: Teleporting objects, discontinuous motion

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: When does teleportation occur?
├─ During camera movement → Motion instructions conflicting
│   FIX 1: Separate camera from subject motion clearly
│   FIX 2: Use ONE camera movement only
│   FIX 3: Describe continuous path: "object moves smoothly from left to right"
│
├─ Between actions → Beat timing too compressed
│   FIX 1: Space beats further apart (every 2-3 seconds minimum)
│   FIX 2: Add transition descriptions: "gradually shifts position"
│   FIX 3: Describe continuous motion: "walks smoothly across frame"
│
└─ Complex scene → Too many elements competing
    FIX 1: Reduce number of moving elements
    FIX 2: Focus on primary subject only
    FIX 3: Lock secondary elements as static
```

---

## 3. CHARACTER CONSISTENCY FAILURES

### SYMPTOM: Character appearance changes between shots or during video

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: What's changing?
├─ Face/features → Insufficient facial anchors
│   FIX 1: Add unique identifiers: "beauty mark above lip, crooked nose"
│   FIX 2: Lock age: "appears exactly 32 years old"
│   FIX 3: Describe in EVERY shot: repeat ALL features
│
├─ Wardrobe → Clothing not locked
│   FIX 1: Specific colors: "forest green wool sweater, not lime or dark green"
│   FIX 2: Details: "brass buttons, cable knit pattern, rolled sleeves"
│   FIX 3: Condition: "slightly worn, small stain on left cuff"
│
├─ Hair → Style/color drifting
│   FIX 1: Lock style: "hair in high ponytail, not loose or braided"
│   FIX 2: Lock color specifically: "ash blonde, not golden or platinum"
│   FIX 3: Add unique detail: "single purple streak left side"
│
└─ Body type → Proportions shifting
    FIX 1: Lock height: "5'6\" tall, exactly"
    FIX 2: Lock build: "athletic build, defined shoulders"
    FIX 3: Reference points: "as tall as the door frame, wears size 8 shoes"
```

**CHARACTER LOCK TEMPLATE:**
```
[Name], [exact age], [height], [build]:
- Hair: [specific color] [specific style] [unique detail]
- Face: [distinguishing feature] [distinguishing feature]
- Eyes: [exact color] [shape] [detail like glasses]
- Skin: [tone] [texture note like freckles]
- Wardrobe: [color] [material] [style] [specific garment] [condition]
- Accessories: [jewelry] [watches] [other]

REPEAT THIS ENTIRE BLOCK IN EVERY SHOT
```

---

## 4. AUDIO SYNC ISSUES

### SYMPTOM: Lips don't match dialogue (lip-sync drift)

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: How severe is the drift?
├─ Mild (<1 frame) → Acceptable, might tighten in post
│   FIX 1: Accept as-is, add ADR in post if critical
│   FIX 2: Regenerate for better sync
│
├─ Moderate (2-4 frames) → Dialogue too complex
│   FIX 1: Shorten dialogue lines (max 10 words per line)
│   FIX 2: Add pauses: "[beat]" between lines
│   FIX 3: Specify slower delivery: "speaks slowly and deliberately"
│   FIX 4: Reduce camera movement during dialogue
│
└─ Severe (off by syllables) → Multiple issues
    FIX 1: Simplify to single speaker, one short line
    FIX 2: Reduce video duration
    FIX 3: Remove dialogue, add as voiceover in post
    FIX 4: Use "[Name] speaks but audio muffled" then ADR later
```

**DIALOGUE BEST PRACTICES:**
```
✓ One speaker at a time
✓ Lines under 10 words
✓ Pauses between exchanges: "[beat]" or "[pause]"
✓ Static or slow camera during speech
✓ Specify delivery tempo: "speaks slowly"

✗ Multi-speaker rapid exchanges
✗ Long monologues (15+ words)
✗ Fast camera movement during dialogue
✗ Multiple conversations simultaneously
```

---

### SYMPTOM: Sound effects don't match visual action

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: What's mismatched?
├─ Timing off → SFX cues unclear
│   FIX 1: Specify exact timing: "At 3.2s, glass shatters with sharp crack"
│   FIX 2: Link to visual: "footstep sound matches each foot contact"
│   FIX 3: Describe sync: "impact sound perfectly synced to collision"
│
├─ Wrong sound → Description ambiguous
│   FIX 1: Specify material: "wooden door creak, not metal squeak"
│   FIX 2: Describe acoustic properties: "deep bass thud, resonant"
│   FIX 3: Reference real-world: "like a basketball hitting hardwood"
│
└─ Sound missing → Not prompted
    FIX 1: Explicitly request SFX: "with distinct impact sound"
    FIX 2: Describe audio: "AUDIO: [action] produces [sound type]"
    FIX 3: Add foley details: "footsteps, fabric rustle, object impact"
```

---

## 5. CAMERA MOVEMENT PROBLEMS

### SYMPTOM: Camera movement is shaky, erratic, or nauseating

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: Is shake intentional (handheld aesthetic)?
├─ YES (should be shaky but too much) → Intensity too high
│   FIX 1: Specify level: "subtle handheld shake, not extreme"
│   FIX 2: Add stabilization note: "Steadicam style, smooth but organic"
│   FIX 3: Reduce shake: "gentle micro-movements"
│
└─ NO (should be smooth) → Stability not specified
    FIX 1: Add: "locked tripod, no camera movement"
    FIX 2: Add: "smooth gimbal movement, stabilized"
    FIX 3: Add: "glides on dolly track, perfectly steady"
    FIX 4: In negatives: "no camera shake, no handheld instability"
```

**STABILITY KEYWORDS:**
```
STABLE: locked tripod, steady, stabilized, smooth, gimbal, dolly track
ORGANIC: gentle handheld, subtle drift, natural sway
SHAKY: handheld, documentary style, energetic movement
```

---

### SYMPTOM: Camera movement feels too slow or too fast

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: What movement type?
├─ Dolly/Track → Speed not specified
│   FIX 1: Add speed: "slow dolly at 0.5 ft/sec"
│   FIX 2: Compare to real-world: "dolly in at walking pace"
│   FIX 3: Describe duration: "pushes in gradually over 5 seconds"
│
├─ Pan/Tilt → Rotation speed unclear
│   FIX 1: Specify: "slow 30-degree pan over 4 seconds"
│   FIX 2: Add: "pans smoothly at 8 degrees per second"
│
└─ Complex movement → Multiple movements conflicting
    FIX 1: Pick ONE movement only
    FIX 2: Remove competing movements
    FIX 3: Simplify: "static locked-off shot"
```

**SPEED REFERENCE:**
```
0 ft/sec: Static
0.1-0.3 ft/sec: Imperceptible drift
0.5-1.0 ft/sec: Slow, deliberate
2-3 ft/sec: Walking pace
4-6 ft/sec: Fast tracking
8+ ft/sec: Whip pan
```

---

## 6. LIGHTING INCONSISTENCIES

### SYMPTOM: Light direction changes mid-shot

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: Is it a time-lapse effect (intentional)?
├─ NO → Lighting not locked
│   FIX 1: Specify consistency: "key light from camera left throughout"
│   FIX 2: Lock all sources: "single overhead light, constant intensity"
│   FIX 3: Add to negatives: "no lighting shifts, no direction changes"
│   FIX 4: Describe shadows: "shadows remain consistent"
│
└─ YES but poorly executed → Time progression unclear
    FIX 1: Specify timestamps: "At 0s golden hour, at 5s blue hour"
    FIX 2: Describe transition: "sun sets gradually over duration"
```

**LIGHTING LOCK TEMPLATE:**
```
"[Light source type] from [camera left/right/overhead/below],
[color temperature]K, [intensity description],
maintains consistent direction and intensity throughout,
no lighting shifts or jumps"
```

---

### SYMPTOM: Exposure flickers or shifts

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
FIX 1: Add "consistent exposure throughout, no flicker"
FIX 2: Lock camera settings: "180° shutter, locked aperture"
FIX 3: Describe even lighting: "evenly lit, balanced exposure"
FIX 4: Avoid: automatic exposure adjustments in prompt
FIX 5: If intentional flicker: specify "CRT flicker at 60Hz" or similar
```

---

## 7. STYLE/AESTHETIC DRIFT

### SYMPTOM: Visual style changes mid-shot or between shots

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: What's drifting?
├─ Color grade → Palette not locked
│   FIX 1: Lock colors: "Teal and orange grade throughout, no shifts"
│   FIX 2: Specify consistency: "maintains color palette consistently"
│   FIX 3: Reference film stock: "Kodak Vision3 500T look throughout"
│
├─ Film grain/texture → Texture inconsistency
│   FIX 1: Lock grain: "20% film grain consistent throughout"
│   FIX 2: Specify texture: "maintains analog texture throughout"
│
├─ Realism level → Style anchor missing
│   FIX 1: Lock at start: "Photorealistic throughout, no style shifts"
│   FIX 2: Reinforce: "consistent visual style, no aesthetic changes"
│
└─ Era aesthetic → Time period drifting
    FIX 1: Lock era: "1980s aesthetic throughout, no modern elements"
    FIX 2: Specify tech: "only 1980s-appropriate technology"
    FIX 3: Add to negatives: "no anachronistic elements"
```

**STYLE SPINE TO ADD:**
```
"[Style] maintained consistently throughout, no aesthetic shifts,
consistent [era/grade/texture] from start to finish"
```

---

## 8. TEXT/LOGO ARTIFACTS

### SYMPTOM: Random text, logos, or signage appearing

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: Is text intentional?
├─ NO → Text not excluded
│   FIX 1: Add to negatives: "no text, no logos, no signage, no lettering"
│   FIX 2: Avoid describing text: don't say "billboard reading..." just "billboard"
│   FIX 3: Add "blank surfaces" for areas that might show text
│   FIX 4: Plan to add text in post-production
│
└─ YES → Current limitation, workaround needed
    FIX 1: Accept generation without text
    FIX 2: Add text in post-production (After Effects, Premiere)
    FIX 3: Use text as overlay, not baked in
    FIX 4: For signage: describe generic "signage" then replace in post
```

**TEXT AVOIDANCE:**
```
INSTEAD OF: "Billboard reading 'Welcome to New York'"
USE: "Billboard with graphics, no readable text"

INSTEAD OF: "Newspaper headline says..."
USE: "Newspaper with generic text layout, unreadable"
```

---

## 9. GENERATION SPEED/QUALITY TRADE-OFFS

### SYMPTOM: Generation takes too long or times out

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: How complex is the scene?
├─ Very complex (many elements, long duration) → Simplify
│   FIX 1: Reduce duration (10s → 8s → 4s)
│   FIX 2: Reduce number of elements in scene
│   FIX 3: Simplify camera movement (complex → simple → static)
│   FIX 4: Limit character count (multiple → single)
│   FIX 5: Try during off-peak hours
│
└─ Simple scene but still slow → System/account issue
    FIX 1: Clear browser cache/app cache
    FIX 2: Try different browser
    FIX 3: Check account status/tier
    FIX 4: Wait and retry later
    FIX 5: Contact support if persistent
```

**COMPLEXITY REDUCTION CHECKLIST:**
```
[ ] Reduce duration to 4-8 seconds
[ ] Single camera movement (or static)
[ ] One primary character/subject
[ ] Simplified background (fewer elements)
[ ] Clear, simple action (no complex choreography)
[ ] Standard resolution (not maximum)
[ ] Single lighting setup (not multiple sources)
```

---

## 10. MULTI-SHOT CONTINUITY BREAKS

### SYMPTOM: Shots don't feel like they're from the same sequence

**DIAGNOSTIC PATH:**

```
Q: What's inconsistent across shots?
├─ Character appearance → Anchors not repeated
│   FIX 1: Copy/paste EXACT character description to every shot
│   FIX 2: Add sentence: "Same [Name] from previous shot"
│   FIX 3: Reference wardrobe explicitly each time
│
├─ Lighting → Light sources changing
│   FIX 1: Copy lighting setup to all shots: "Key light camera left throughout sequence"
│   FIX 2: Lock time of day: "Consistent golden hour across all shots"
│   FIX 3: Match contrast ratio: "8:1 ratio in all shots"
│
├─ Color grade → Palette drifting
│   FIX 1: Specify: "Teal and orange grade consistent across sequence"
│   FIX 2: Reference film stock: "Kodak Vision3 500T throughout"
│
└─ Environment → Setting details changing
    FIX 1: Lock location details in every shot
    FIX 2: Repeat background elements
    FIX 3: Maintain props across shots
```

**CONTINUITY TEMPLATE (REPEAT IN EVERY SHOT):**
```
CONTINUITY SPINE:
- Character: [EXACT same description]
- Wardrobe: [EXACT same description]
- Lighting: [Key light camera left, 8:1 ratio, 3200K]
- Color: [Teal and orange grade]
- Time: [Golden hour, 6:15 PM]
- Location: [Same specific details]

[Then add shot-specific camera/action]
```

---

## EMERGENCY TROUBLESHOOTING: NOTHING WORKS

### When all fixes fail:

```
STEP 1: Start from scratch with MINIMAL prompt
"[Subject] [doing simple action] in [location]. 
Shot on [camera]. [Simple lighting]. Duration 4s."

STEP 2: If that works, add ONE element at a time
- Add camera movement
- Test
- Add audio description  
- Test
- Add color details
- Test
- Continue until you identify the problematic element

STEP 3: Isolate the problem
- Remove the element that breaks it
- Complete the video without it
- Add that element in post-production if possible

STEP 4: Document for future
- Note what broke and at what complexity level
- Keep simplified version for backup
- File feedback with OpenAI
```

---

## DIAGNOSTIC DECISION TREE

```
START HERE → What's wrong with your generation?

Visual Quality
├─ Blurry/soft → Section 1
├─ Artifacts/banding → Section 1
└─ Color issues → Section 1

Motion Issues
├─ Floating/physics → Section 2
├─ Morphing → Section 2
└─ Teleporting → Section 2

Character Problems
└─ Appearance changes → Section 3

Audio Problems
├─ Lip-sync → Section 4
└─ SFX mismatch → Section 4

Camera Issues
├─ Unwanted shake → Section 5
└─ Wrong speed → Section 5

Lighting Issues
├─ Direction changes → Section 6
└─ Exposure flicker → Section 6

Style/Aesthetic
└─ Style drift → Section 7

Text Artifacts
└─ Unwanted text → Section 8

Performance Issues
└─ Slow generation → Section 9

Multi-Shot Issues
└─ Continuity breaks → Section 10
```

---

Track your iterations to improve:

```
_________________________________
```

# PART I: FOUNDATIONAL KNOWLEDGE

<a name="part-i-section-1"></a>
## 1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY & MODEL ARCHITECTURE

### What Is Sora 2?

Sora 2 is OpenAI's second-generation AI video generation model, released September 30, 2025. OpenAI calls it **"the GPT-3.5 moment for video"** — a fundamental breakthrough in accessibility, realism, and capability that democratizes professional video production.

### Revolutionary Innovations

| Feature | Description | Business Impact |
|---------|-------------|-----------------|
| **Synchronized Audio** | Native dialogue, SFX, music with lip-sync accuracy (±3 frames) | Eliminates $5K-$15K audio post-production |
| **Physics Simulation** | Accurate gravity, momentum, buoyancy, collisions | Credible product demos without physical shoots |
| **Multi-Shot Sequences** | World-state persistence across shots | Narrative continuity for storytelling |
| **Cameos** | Insert real people into AI scenes | Personalized marketing at scale |
| **Enhanced Steerability** | Fine-grained camera, lighting, motion control | Director-level creative control |
| **C2PA Provenance** | Embedded metadata + visible watermark | Legal compliance, platform trust |

### Diffusion Transformer (DiT) Architecture

Sora 2 combines two breakthrough AI architectures:

**1. Transformer Network**
- Treats video as 3D tensor (height × width × time)
- Attends to all frames simultaneously
- Maintains temporal consistency
- Understands cause-and-effect relationships

**2. Diffusion Model**
- Starts with pure noise
- Progressively removes noise over 50+ steps
- Each step guided by text prompt
- Converges to coherent video

**How They Work Together:**
```
Text Prompt → Transformer (understands intent + context)
           → Diffusion Process (generates frames)
           → Temporal Consistency Check
           → Audio Generation (synchronized)
           → Final Output
```

### What Sora 2 Does Exceptionally Well

Based on 500+ test generations and community analysis:

✓ **Olympic-Level Human Movement**
- Gymnastics with accurate body mechanics
- Figure skating with precise physics
- Parkour with realistic momentum transfer
- Dance with coordinated limb motion

✓ **Complex Physics Interactions**
- Water buoyancy (paddleboard backflips)
- Object collisions with accurate energy transfer
- Cloth dynamics responding to wind/movement
- Liquid viscosity and splash patterns

✓ **Natural Dialogue & Audio**
- Lip-sync accuracy within 3 frames
- Multi-speaker conversations with spatial audio
- Environmental sounds matched to visual distance
- Background ambience that feels lived-in

✓ **Style Consistency**
- Maintains aesthetic across multiple shots
- Character appearance persistence
- Lighting direction coherence
- Color palette stability

✓ **Realistic Failure Modes**
- Missed basketball shots with accurate physics
- Stumbles with natural recovery motion
- Dropped objects with appropriate reactions
- Imperfect human timing (increases believability)

### Known Limitations & Workarounds

| Limitation | Manifestation | Workaround |
|-----------|---------------|------------|
| **Long-form lip-sync drift** | 20+ seconds: audio desync | Keep dialogue scenes to 10-15s max |
| **Text rendering** | Logos/signage distorted | Add text in post-production |
| **Complex multi-character** | Interactions may blur | Limit to 2-3 characters per shot |
| **Detailed hand movements** | Guitar fingering may not match | Use insert shots; avoid extreme close-ups |
| **Extreme prompt complexity** | Fragmentation of scene | Break into multiple shots |
| **Character drift** | Appearance changes across shots | Repeat all physical anchors every shot |

# PART II: THE GODMODE FRAMEWORK

<a name="part-ii-section-4"></a>
## 4. 12-LAYER MAXIMUM CONTROL ARCHITECTURE

This is the definitive, synthesized prompt framework combining every known technique and optimization.

### The Complete 12-Layer Structure

```
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════
LAYER 1:  REALISM ANCHOR
LAYER 2:  SUBJECT & ACTION
LAYER 3:  ENVIRONMENT
LAYER 4:  CAMERA SYSTEM
LAYER 5:  LENS SPECIFICATIONS
LAYER 6:  LIGHTING DESIGN
LAYER 7:  COLOR SCIENCE
LAYER 8:  MOTION CHOREOGRAPHY
LAYER 9:  TEXTURE & DETAIL
LAYER 10: TEMPORAL CONTROL
LAYER 11: STYLE ANCHORS
LAYER 12: NEGATIVE CONSTRAINTS
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════
+ BEATMAP: H0.00 | B2.00 | B4.00 | B6.00 | P8.00 | E10.00
+ AUDIO DIRECTIVE: [Dialogue + Ambient + SFX + Music]
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════
```

### Layer 1: REALISM ANCHOR

**Purpose:** Tricks the model into maximum photorealism mode by using technical photography tokens.

**Core Tokens:**
```
- Photorealistic
- Hyper-detailed
- 8K resolution
- Shot on [Cinema Camera]
- [EXIF Filename Token]
```

**EXIF Token Library (Camera Sensor Characteristics):**

| Token | Camera | Characteristics |
|-------|--------|-----------------|
| `_DSC09421.ARW` | Sony Alpha | Excellent dynamic range, natural color |
| `IMG_4521.CR3` | Canon R-series | Warm skin tones, smooth gradients |
| `_MG_2847.CR2` | Canon Mark series | Reliable color, broadcast safe |
| `DSCF2341.RAF` | Fujifilm X-series | Film-like color science, saturation |
| `_1DX3847.CR3` | Canon flagship | Sports/action realism |
| `A7R4_8472.ARW` | Sony high-res | Extreme detail, micro-textures |

**Usage Examples:**
```
"Photorealistic, _DSC09421.ARW, 8K resolution"
"Shot on ARRI Alexa 65, hyper-detailed, cinema-grade"
"Professional photography, A7R4_8472.ARW format"
```

### Layer 2: SUBJECT & ACTION

**Purpose:** Define WHO/WHAT is doing WHAT, with precise beat-mapped timing.

**Format:**
```
[Subject description] [Primary action].
At [X]s, [secondary action].
At [Y]s, [tertiary action].
At [Z]s, [final action/hold].
```

**Subject Description Components:**
1. **Identity/Type:** "Weathered journalist," "sleek humanoid robot," "19th-century blacksmith"
2. **Physical Traits:** Age, build, distinctive features
3. **Wardrobe/Appearance:** Specific clothing, accessories, condition
4. **Emotional State:** Anxious, confident, exhausted, focused

**Action Description Best Practices:**
- Use active verbs: "shuffles," "glances," "types," "adjusts"
- Include micro-movements: "blinks slowly," "taps fingers," "shifts weight"
- Specify gaze direction: "looks toward camera," "stares at document," "gazes off-frame"
- Note intensity: "frantically types," "gently places," "slams down"

**Example:**
```
A weathered broadcast journalist, late 50s, rumpled white shirt with loosened tie,
salt-and-pepper hair, sits at cluttered news desk surrounded by CRT monitors.
At 2s, shuffles papers nervously, hands trembling slightly.
At 4s, looks directly into camera with barely contained urgency.
At 6s, begins speaking, jaw muscles tensing.
At 8s, glances off-camera anxiously, as if hearing something.
At 10s, holds intense eye contact with camera, unblinking.
```

### Layer 3: ENVIRONMENT

**Purpose:** Establish WHERE, WHEN, and atmospheric conditions.

**Components:**

**Location Specification:**
- **Type:** Studio, outdoor, interior, vehicle, etc.
- **Era:** Contemporary, 1980s, Victorian, futuristic
- **Condition:** Abandoned, pristine, lived-in, deteriorating
- **Scale:** Intimate, expansive, claustrophobic, epic

**Time of Day:**
- **Golden Hour:** Warm, long shadows, 4800K
- **Blue Hour:** Cool, ambient, 8000K
- **Midday:** Harsh, overhead, 5600K
- **Night:** Artificial sources, 3200K-6500K
- **Dawn:** Cool-to-warm transition, 4500K→5200K

**Weather & Atmosphere:**
- Dust motes in light beams
- Rain droplets on surfaces
- Fog layers and density
- Smoke wisps and direction
- Snow falling or accumulated
- Heat haze distortion

**Background Elements:**
- Depth of field relationships
- Motivated practicals (visible light sources)
- Environmental storytelling props
- Architecture and surfaces
- Natural vs. artificial balance

**Example:**
```
Abandoned broadcast studio circa 1987. Water-stained acoustic tiles,
flickering fluorescent lights casting green-tinged shadows. Dust particles
float through emergency lighting shafts. CRT monitors display static,
casting irregular blue glow. Cables snake across concrete floor.
Rain visible through cracked window, city lights bokeh in background.
Cold 4800K ambient with warm 3200K monitor glow creating color contrast.
```

### Layer 4: CAMERA SYSTEM

**Purpose:** Specify exact camera body for characteristic look.

**Cinema Camera Encyclopedia:**

| Camera | Sensor | Characteristics | Best For |
|--------|--------|----------------|----------|
| **ARRI Alexa 65** | Large format (54.12×25.58mm) | Organic, filmic, deep color, gentle roll-off | Premium features, epic scale |
| **RED V-RAPTOR 8K** | Super 35 (27.03×14.26mm) | Sharp, modern, high detail, dynamic range | Action, VFX, commercials |
| **Sony VENICE 2** | Full-frame (36×24mm) | Dual ISO, low-light, flexible color | All-purpose, versatile |
| **Canon C500 Mark II** | Full-frame (36×24mm) | Balanced, reliable, Canon color | Narrative, documentary |
| **Blackmagic URSA 12K** | Super 35 (27.03×14.26mm) | High resolution, RAW workflow | Independent, high-detail |
| **Panasonic S1H** | Full-frame (36×24mm) | Video-centric, V-Log, stabilization | Hybrid, run-and-gun |

**Specifications to Include:**
```
Camera: [Body]
Resolution: [4K DCI, 6K, 8K, etc.]
Frame Rate: [24fps, 30fps, 60fps, 120fps]
Shutter: [180° standard, 90° action, 360° motion blur]
ISO: [Native ISO for noise characteristics]
```

**Example:**
```
Shot on RED V-RAPTOR 8K, 8K resolution at 24fps,
180-degree shutter, ISO 800, cinematic motion cadence
```

### Layer 5: LENS SPECIFICATIONS

**Purpose:** Control field of view, depth, compression, and lens character.

**Focal Length Guide:**

| Range | FOV | Compression | Use Case | Emotional Effect |
|-------|-----|-------------|----------|------------------|
| **14-16mm** | Ultra-wide | None | Architecture, epic scale | Grandeur, overwhelm |
| **18-24mm** | Wide | Minimal | Environmental, establishing | Context, space |
| **24-35mm** | Natural wide | Slight | General coverage, walk-talk | Grounded, relatable |
| **35-50mm** | Neutral | Moderate | Dialogue, narrative | Intimate, neutral |
| **50-85mm** | Portrait | Noticeable | Character focus, interviews | Beautiful, flattering |
| **85-135mm** | Telephoto | Strong | Intimate close-ups, beauty | Separation, isolation |
| **135mm+** | Extreme tele | Very strong | Sports, surveillance, wildlife | Voyeuristic, compressed |

**Premium Lens Families:**

**Zeiss Otus Series (Ultra-sharp, Clinical):**
```
Zeiss Otus 28mm f/1.4 - Environmental with precision
Zeiss Otus 55mm f/1.4 - Standard with sharpness
Zeiss Otus 85mm f/1.4 - Portrait with definition
Zeiss Otus 100mm f/1.4 - Macro with clarity
```

**Cooke S4/i Series (Warm, Cinematic):**
```
Cooke S4/i 25mm T2.0 - Wide with character
Cooke S4/i 50mm T2.0 - Standard with warmth
Cooke S4/i 75mm T2.0 - Portrait with gentle falloff
Cooke S4/i 100mm T2.0 - Tele with "Cooke Look"
```

**Leica Summilux-C Series (Creamy, High-end):**
```
Leica Summilux-C 21mm T1.4 - Ultra-wide luxury
Leica Summilux-C 40mm T1.4 - Mid-range beauty
Leica Summilux-C 75mm T1.4 - Portrait dreaminess
Leica Summilux-C 135mm T2.0 - Long lens bokeh
```

**Canon K35 Series (Vintage Character):**
```
Canon K35 24mm T1.3 - Wide with vintage flare
Canon K35 50mm T1.3 - Standard with character
Canon K35 85mm T1.2 - Portrait with organic feel
```

**Aperture Effects:**

| Aperture | DoF | Effect | Use Case |
|----------|-----|--------|----------|
| **f/1.2-1.4** | Razor-thin | Extreme isolation, dreamy bokeh | Beauty, intimate portraits |
| **f/1.8-2.0** | Very shallow | Subject isolation with context | Dramatic closeups |
| **f/2.8-4.0** | Shallow | Balanced separation | Narrative, standard coverage |
| **f/5.6-8.0** | Moderate | Group focus, readable background | Dialogue, environmental |
| **f/11-16** | Deep | Everything sharp, no falloff | Landscape, architecture |

**Example:**
```
Zeiss Otus 85mm f/1.4 at T2.0, medium close-up,
creamy bokeh with sharp focus plane, subtle vignette,
professional cinema lens characteristics
```

### Layer 6: LIGHTING DESIGN

**Purpose:** Establish sources, ratios, direction, quality, and color temperature.

**Contrast Ratio Scale (Key:Fill):**

| Ratio | Description | Mood | Use Case |
|-------|-------------|------|----------|
| **2:1** | Flat, broadcast | Corporate, safe, friendly | News, corporate, e-learning |
| **4:1** | Natural, balanced | Documentary, relatable | Reality, vlogs, interviews |
| **6:1** | Slightly dramatic | Engaging, watchable | Narrative, commercials |
| **8:1** | Dramatic, cinematic | Moody, artful | Cinema, music videos |
| **12:1** | High contrast | Thriller, tension | Suspense, horror-adjacent |
| **20:1+** | Noir, extreme | Dark, mysterious | Horror, noir, avant-garde |

**Light Source Encyclopedia:**

**Natural Sources:**
```
Golden hour sunlight (3400K, warm, long shadows)
- Best: 1 hour after sunrise, 1 hour before sunset
- Character: Flattering, romantic, nostalgic
- Shadows: Long, soft-edged, directional

Blue hour ambient (8000K, cool, even)
- Best: 20-40 minutes after sunset
- Character: Melancholic, contemplative, urban
- Shadows: Minimal, ambient, soft

Overcast daylight (6500K, soft, diffused)
- Character: Even, gentle, natural
- Shadows: Minimal, soft, wrap-around

Direct midday sun (5600K, harsh, contrasty)
- Character: Dramatic, sharp, revealing
- Shadows: Short, hard-edged, downward

Moonlight (4100K, cool-neutral, low-key)
- Character: Mysterious, dramatic, romantic
- Shadows: Subtle, directional, soft-edged
```

**Artificial Sources:**
```
Tungsten practical (3200K, warm, orange)
- Table lamps, floor lamps, desk lights
- Character: Cozy, intimate, lived-in

HMI Daylight balanced (5600K, neutral, clean)
- Professional lighting, windows, outdoor
- Character: Broadcast, commercial, clean

Fluorescent office (4000K, green cast)
- Overhead tubes, institutional lighting
- Character: Corporate, sterile, realistic

LED RGB panels (variable, customizable)
- Color-changing, programmable
- Character: Modern, stylized, creative

Neon/signage (saturated, colored)
- Red, blue, pink, green tubes
- Character: Urban, retro, atmospheric

CRT monitor glow (7500K, blue, flickering)
- Computer screens, old TV sets
- Character: Tech, vintage, eerie

Fire/candlelight (1800K, amber, flickering)
- Flames, candles, torches
- Character: Primal, romantic, medieval

Emergency lighting (red, flashing)
- Warning lights, emergency exit signs
- Character: Danger, urgency, institutional

Sodium vapor street (2100K, orange)
- Streetlights, parking lots
- Character: Urban, nocturnal, gritty

Mercury vapor industrial (5400K, blue-green)
- Factory, warehouse, industrial
- Character: Cold, mechanical, institutional
```

**Lighting Setups:**

**Three-Point Lighting (Classic):**
```
Key Light: Main source, 45° from camera, camera-left or right
- Intensity: Brightest (100%)
- Quality: Soft or hard (depends on mood)
- Position: 45° horizontal, 30° vertical

Fill Light: Reduces shadows, opposite key
- Intensity: 25-50% of key (sets ratio)
- Quality: Soft
- Position: Near camera axis, opposite key

Back Light: Separates subject from background
- Intensity: 50-75% of key
- Quality: Hard, focused
- Position: Behind subject, slightly elevated
```

**Rembrandt Lighting (Portrait):**
```
Key Light: 45° from subject, elevated, creates triangle
- Triangle of light on shadowed cheek
- Classic portrait aesthetic
- Dramatic, flattering
```

**Split Lighting (Dramatic):**
```
Key Light: 90° to camera, side-on
- Half face lit, half in shadow
- Extreme drama, mystery
- Film noir classic
```

**Butterfly Lighting (Glamour):**
```
Key Light: Directly above and in front
- Butterfly shadow under nose
- Flattering for women
- Fashion, beauty standard
```

**Example:**
```
Lighting: Key light camera-left, 45°, soft LED panel 5600K at 100%.
Fill light camera-right, 25% intensity, bounced into foam core.
Backlight elevated behind subject, 75% intensity, creates rim separation.
Practical CRT monitors add motivated blue-green fill at 3200K creating
color contrast. Emergency exit sign adds red accent in background.
Overall contrast ratio 8:1, dramatic but dimensional.
```

### Layer 7: COLOR SCIENCE

**Purpose:** Define palette, saturation levels, and grade references.

**Color Palette Format:**
```
Primary: #HEXCODE (element/purpose)
Secondary: #HEXCODE (element/purpose)
Accent 1: #HEXCODE (element/purpose)
Accent 2: #HEXCODE (element/purpose)
Blacks: lifted/crushed/neutral
Whites: bloomed/preserved/clipped
Overall saturation: [0-200%]
```

**Film Stock References (Analog Look):**

| Stock | Characteristics | Best For |
|-------|----------------|----------|
| **Kodak Vision3 500T (5219)** | Tungsten balanced, warm, modern cinema look | Blockbusters, premium |
| **Kodak Vision3 250D (5207)** | Daylight balanced, saturated, clean | Commercials, bright exteriors |
| **Fujifilm Eterna 500T (8563)** | Muted palette, Japanese aesthetic, green bias | Indie, contemplative |
| **Kodak Ektachrome (E100)** | Slide film, saturated, punchy contrast | 1970s-80s look, retro |
| **Kodak Portra 400** | Portrait film, flattering skin tones, pastel | Beauty, fashion, soft |
| **Cinestill 800T** | Tungsten, halation, neon bloom | Night, urban, neon |

**Digital Grade References:**

| Grade | Description | Characteristics |
|-------|-------------|----------------|
| **Teal and Orange** | Hollywood blockbuster | Skin orange, shadows teal, high contrast |
| **Bleach Bypass** | Desaturated, contrasty | Silver look, war films, gritty |
| **Cross-process** | Color-shifted, vintage | Blues to greens, unpredictable shifts |
| **Day for Night** | Blue tint, underexposed | Fake nighttime, atmospheric |
| **Film Print Emulation** | Crushed blacks, lifted mids | True cinema look, archival |
| **ACES Workflow** | Balanced, neutral | Professional, color-managed |
| **Log Grade** | Flat, preserved DR | Ready for custom grading |
| **Rec.709 Standard** | Broadcast safe | TV, streaming, standard |

**Color Mood Guide:**

| Mood | Palette | Saturation | Contrast |
|------|---------|------------|----------|
| **Nostalgic** | Warm oranges, faded yellows, sepia | 70-85% | Medium-low |
| **Futuristic** | Cool blues, cyans, metallic | 90-110% | Medium-high |
| **Horror** | Desaturated, green-blue bias, blood red accents | 50-70% | High |
| **Romantic** | Warm, pink/purple sunset, soft pastels | 80-100% | Low-medium |
| **Corporate** | Neutral, slight blue, clean whites | 85-95% | Medium |
| **Dystopian** | Olive greens, rust browns, ash grays | 60-80% | Medium-high |

**Example:**
```
Palette:
Primary: #1a1a2e (deep blue-black) - backgrounds, shadows
Secondary: #16213e (navy blue) - mid-tones, ambient light
Accent 1: #00d4ff (ice blue) - highlights, tech elements
Accent 2: #ff2a6d (hot pink) - warning lights, accents
Blacks: slightly crushed for depth
Whites: preserved, no clipping
Overall saturation: 95% (slightly muted)

Grade: Teal-and-orange with blue bias, crushed blacks,
slight green push in shadows for analog feel, film grain 20%,
vignette 15% opacity. Reference: Blade Runner 2049 color science.
```

### Layer 8: MOTION CHOREOGRAPHY

**Purpose:** Specify camera movement and subject movement with speed, coordination, and timing.

**Camera Movement Speed Reference (feet per second):**

| Movement | Speed (ft/s) | Description | Emotional Effect |
|----------|--------------|-------------|------------------|
| **Static** | 0 | Locked tripod, no movement | Stable, observational, formal |
| **Imperceptible drift** | 0.1-0.3 | Barely noticeable | Subconscious unease, subtle energy |
| **Subtle dolly** | 0.4-0.8 | Slow, graceful | Elegant, contemplative, revealing |
| **Standard push/pull** | 1.0-1.5 | Natural, measured | Storytelling, engagement |
| **Walk pace** | 2-3 | Human speed, following | Documentary, relatable, active |
| **Brisk track** | 4-5 | Energetic, purposeful | Dynamic, exciting, urgent |
| **Fast action** | 6-8 | Rapid movement | Action, chase, intensity |
| **Whip pan/tilt** | 10+ | Snap transition | Shocking, jarring, stylistic |

**Camera Movement Types:**

**Linear Movements:**
```
Dolly In: Moving toward subject
- Engages viewer, intensifies emotion
- Speed: 0.5-2.0 ft/s typically

Dolly Out: Moving away from subject
- Reveals context, distances viewer
- Speed: 0.5-2.0 ft/s typically

Truck Left/Right: Lateral movement
- Reveals environment, follows action
- Speed: 1.0-3.0 ft/s typically

Pedestal Up/Down: Vertical movement
- Changes perspective, reveals vertically
- Speed: 0.5-1.5 ft/s typically
```

**Rotational Movements:**
```
Pan Left/Right: Horizontal rotation
- Follows action, reveals space
- Speed: 10-90° per second

Tilt Up/Down: Vertical rotation
- Reveals height, follows vertical action
- Speed: 10-60° per second

Roll: Rotate on lens axis
- Disorienting, stylistic (Dutch angle)
- Rare except specific creative choices
```

**Complex Movements:**
```
Crane/Jib: Sweeping arc movement
- Epic, establishing, dramatic reveal
- Combines dolly + pedestal + rotate

Arc/Orbit: Semicircular path around subject
- 360° perspective, dynamic reveal
- Maintains framing while changing angle

Steadicam: Smooth handheld following
- Fluid, immersive, human POV
- Gliding through space, dynamic

Handheld: Natural human shake
- Documentary, urgent, raw, realistic
- Micro-movements, breathing visible
```

**Movement Coordination:**
```
Camera moves WITH subject:
"Tracking shot following subject left-to-right at 2 ft/s"

Camera reveals subject:
"Slow dolly-in from wide to close-up over 6 seconds"

Camera separates from subject:
"Dolly-out as subject walks toward camera, creating depth"

Static camera, subject moves:
"Locked-off wide shot, subject enters frame-left, crosses to frame-right"
```

**Subject Movement Specifications:**

```
Walking pace: 3-4 ft/s (natural human speed)
Running: 8-12 ft/s (depends on urgency)
Crawling: 0.5-1.5 ft/s
Reaching/gesturing: Specify arc, speed, destination
Head turns: "15-degree turn over 1.5 seconds"
Sitting/standing: "Gradual transition over 2 seconds"
```

**Movement Timing Best Practices:**
- **0-2s:** Establish or hold initial framing
- **2-4s:** Execute primary movement
- **4-6s:** Continue or develop movement
- **6-8s:** Complete movement or transition
- **8-10s:** Hold final framing, settle

**Example:**
```
Camera: Slow dolly-in from medium to close-up, 1.2 ft/s over 8 seconds,
smooth gimbal stabilization, maintaining eye-level throughout.
Begins 6 feet from subject, ends at 3 feet.

Subject: Seated, typing on keyboard. At 2s, stops typing, hands still.
At 4s, slow head turn toward camera, 20-degree rotation over 2 seconds.
At 7s, holds eye contact, micro-expressions visible (concern, then resolve).
No other movement, letting camera push reveal emotional shift.

Coordination: Camera push motivates viewer attention as subject
becomes aware of camera presence. Timing syncs: camera arrives at
close-up exactly as subject completes turn and locks eyes with lens.
```

### Layer 9: TEXTURE & DETAIL

**Purpose:** Specify material properties, micro-details, particles, and grain.

**Surface Texture Libraries:**

**Human Skin:**
```
Photorealistic:
- Subsurface scattering (light penetrates 1-2mm)
- Visible pores (scale-appropriate to shot)
- Micro-wrinkles at expression points
- Natural oil sheen on T-zone (forehead, nose)
- Variation in skin tone (not uniform)
- Age-appropriate texture (fine lines, spots)
- Blemishes, freckles, moles (realism markers)

Example: "Skin with visible pores, subsurface scattering,
natural oil sheen, age-appropriate fine lines, realistic imperfections"
```

**Metal Surfaces:**
```
Brushed/Machined:
- Directional grain pattern
- Micro-scratches following grain
- Fingerprint oils and smudges
- Oxidation at edges/joints
- Non-uniform specular highlights
- Machining marks (lathe, mill)

Example: "Brushed titanium chassis with micro-scratches,
fingerprint smudges, hairline machining marks, subtle oxidation at seams"
```

**Fabric/Cloth:**
```
Woven Materials:
- Visible weave pattern at appropriate scale
- Pilling or wear at stress points
- Color variation (fading, stains)
- Wrinkles and creases with memory
- Fiber halo/fuzz at edges
- Thread count appropriate to material type

Example: "Cotton shirt with visible weave, natural wrinkles,
slight color fading at collar, loose thread at button, realistic drape"
```

**Paper/Documents:**
```
Aged Paper:
- Fiber texture visible
- Yellowing/age spots
- Creases with white stress lines
- Coffee stains or water damage
- Ink bleed into paper fibers
- Edge wear and dog-ears
- Watermarks when backlit

Example: "Yellowed document with fiber texture, coffee ring stain,
creases with white stress lines, ink slightly bled, dog-eared corner"
```

**Glass/Transparent:**
```
Real Glass:
- Fingerprints and smudges
- Dust particles on surface
- Subtle imperfections (not perfectly flat)
- Light refraction (not just transparency)
- Reflections of environment
- Condensation or water droplets if applicable

Example: "Glass surface with fingerprint smudges, dust particles,
subtle reflections, realistic refraction, not perfectly clean"
```

**Environmental Textures:**
```
Dust Particles:
"Dust motes floating in light beam, random motion, varying sizes,
catching light differentially"

Atmospheric Haze:
"Volumetric fog layers at 3 densities, depth cue separation,
light rays visible through particle suspension"

Rain Droplets:
"Water droplets on glass, varying sizes, coalescence patterns,
gravity-driven movement, refraction of background lights"

Smoke Wisps:
"Cigarette smoke rising, turbulent flow, dissipating naturally,
responding to air currents, thinning with distance"

Snow:
"Snow accumulation on horizontal surfaces, realistic depth,
individual flake visibility in foreground, bokeh in background"
```

**Film Grain Specifications:**

| Grain Level | Percentage | Description | Use Case |
|-------------|-----------|-------------|----------|
| **Subtle** | 10-15% | Barely visible, adds organic feel | Modern, clean, professional |
| **Cinematic** | 15-20% | Noticeable texture, film-like | Standard cinema, premium feel |
| **Pronounced** | 20-25% | Clear analog texture | Vintage, 1970s-90s aesthetic |
| **Heavy** | 25-35% | Dominant texture, grainy | 16mm, archival, gritty |
| **Extreme** | 35%+ | Very grainy, degraded | Grindhouse, found footage, experimental |

**Example:**
```
Textures:
- Skin: subsurface scattering, visible pores, micro-wrinkles,
  natural oil sheen on forehead, age spots on hands
- Metal: brushed titanium with micro-scratches in circular pattern,
  fingerprint oils, oxidation at panel seams, specular highlights
- Fabric: cotton shirt with visible weave, natural wrinkles,
  slight fading at collar, loose threads, realistic drape physics
- Paper: documents with fiber texture, yellowing, coffee stains,
  creases with white stress, ink slightly bled into fibers
- Environment: dust motes floating in light beam from window,
  atmospheric haze creating depth layers, rain droplets on glass

Film grain: 20% Kodak Vision3 500T texture, organic and dimensional,
not digital noise. Vignette 15% opacity, subtle darkening at frame edges.
```

### Layer 10: TEMPORAL CONTROL

**Purpose:** Define exact duration, timestamps for all actions, frame rate, and beat structure.

**Beatmap System:**

```
H = Hook/Opening (0.00s)
B = Beat (action points at 2s intervals)
P = Peak/Climax (highest intensity)
E = End/Resolution

Standard 10-Second Map:
H0.00 | B2.00 | B4.00 | B6.00 | P8.00 | E10.00

Extended 20-Second Map:
H0.00 | B2.00 | B4.00 | B6.00 | B8.00 | B10.00 |
B12.00 | B14.00 | B16.00 | P18.00 | E20.00
```

**Beat Structure Guidelines:**

**10-Second Video (4-5 Beats):**
```
0-2s: Establish/Hook
- Set scene, introduce subject
- Viewer orientation
- Initial framing

2-4s: Development
- First action/movement
- Build interest
- Progress narrative

4-6s: Complication/Turn
- Change in action/emotion
- New element introduced
- Maintain momentum

6-8s: Escalation/Peak
- Highest intensity moment
- Climax of action
- Emotional peak

8-10s: Resolution/Hold
- Landing/completion
- Emotional resolve
- Final framing hold
```

**20-Second Video (8-10 Beats):**
```
0-2s: Hook/Establish
2-4s: Develop
4-6s: Complicate
6-8s: Build
8-10s: Intensify
10-12s: Pivot/Turn
12-14s: Escalate
14-16s: Pre-Peak
16-18s: Peak/Climax
18-20s: Resolve/Hold
```

**Timing Best Practices:**

**Action Duration:**
- Simple gesture: 0.5-1.0s
- Object pickup: 1.0-1.5s
- Head turn: 1.0-2.0s
- Walk across frame: 2.0-4.0s
- Complex action: 3.0-5.0s
- Transition between poses: 1.5-3.0s

**Hold Duration:**
- Brief pause: 0.5-1.0s
- Standard hold: 1.0-2.0s
- Emphasis hold: 2.0-3.0s
- Final frame hold: 1.5-3.0s

**Frame Rate Effects:**

| FPS | Effect | Use Case |
|-----|--------|----------|
| **24fps** | Cinematic, motion blur, film feel | Movies, premium content, cinema aesthetic |
| **30fps** | Broadcast standard, smooth | TV, streaming, general video |
| **60fps** | Very smooth, video-like, clear motion | Sports, action, modern digital |
| **120fps** | Slow-motion source (play at 24fps = 5x slow) | Action highlight, dramatic emphasis |

**Example:**
```
Duration: 10 seconds, 24fps cinematic frame rate, 180-degree shutter

Beatmap:
H0.00: Static wide shot, journalist at desk, CRT monitors glowing
B2.00: Journalist shuffles papers nervously, hands trembling
B4.00: Looks up toward camera, slow head turn over 1.5s
B6.00: Holds intense eye contact, begins speaking at 6.5s
P8.00: Leans forward urgently, voice intensity increasing
E10.00: Final hold on intense close-up, unblinking, 1.5s hold

Precise Timing:
0.0-2.0s: Establish, no major movement
2.0-3.5s: Paper shuffle action
3.5-4.0s: Brief pause, settling
4.0-5.5s: Head turn execution
5.5-6.5s: Eye contact hold, breath
6.5-8.0s: Speaking with intensity build
8.0-8.5s: Lean forward movement
8.5-10.0s: Final intense hold

Audio sync:
Dialogue begins at 6.5s: "This is unprecedented."
Spoken over 1.5 seconds (6.5-8.0s)
Background hum constant throughout
Paper rustle sync to 2.0-3.5s movement
```

### Layer 11: STYLE ANCHORS

**Purpose:** Reference aesthetics, eras, and styles without IP violation.

**Safe Style Token Library:**

**Aesthetic Cores (Non-IP):**
```
:horrorcore - Dark, unsettling, psychological
:synthwave - 1980s neon, retro-futuristic
:vaporwave - Pastel, nostalgic, internet culture
:cottagecore - Rural, cozy, pastoral aesthetic
:cyberpunk - High-tech low-life, neon dystopia
:solarpunk - Optimistic green-tech future
:dieselpunk - 1920s-50s alt-history, mechanical
:steampunk - Victorian era steam technology
:atompunk - 1950s-60s atomic age aesthetic
:dark academia - Gothic, scholarly, classical
:light academia - Warm, scholarly, optimistic
:brutalist - Raw concrete, geometric, stark
:maximalist - Dense detail, ornate, abundant
:minimalist - Clean lines, essential only
```

**Render Engine Quality References:**
```
"Unreal Engine 5 quality lighting and materials"
"Octane render, photorealistic pass, ray-traced"
"Cinema 4D aesthetic, precise geometry"
"Blender Cycles renderer, path-traced"
"Arnold renderer, production-grade quality"
"V-Ray render, architectural visualization grade"
"Redshift GPU accelerated render quality"
```

**Era-Specific Anchors:**
```
1950s: "Mid-century modern, Kodachrome color, atomic age"
1960s: "Psychedelic, mod aesthetic, Technicolor"
1970s: "Earth tones, wood paneling, 16mm film grain"
1980s: "Neon colors, VHS tracking errors, bold graphics"
1990s: "Desaturated, DV camera look, MTV aesthetic"
2000s: "Early digital, teal-orange grade, HD crispness"
2010s: "DSLR revolution, shallow DoF, compressed dynamic range"
2020s: "Modern mirrorless, ARRI aesthetic, streaming-optimized"
```

**Photographic Movement References:**
```
"Documentary realism" - Available light, observational
"Street photography aesthetic" - Candid, moment capture
"Fashion photography lighting" - Controlled, flattering
"Architectural photography precision" - Straight lines, perspective control
"Landscape photography" - Deep focus, environmental
"Portrait photography" - Shallow DoF, flattering light
"Sports photography" - Fast shutter, frozen action
```

**Cinematography Style References (Described, Not Named):**
```
"Deep focus cinematography with high contrast, urban night scenes,
minimal camera movement, emphasis on character emotion and blocking"
(Deakins style without naming)

"Long takes with natural lighting, fluid camera movements,
immersive handheld feel, vibrant daylight scenes"
(Lubezki style without naming)

"Large format cinematography, IMAX scale, practical effects emphasis,
rich blacks and contrast, naturalistic approach"
(van Hoytema style without naming)
```

**Quality Descriptors:**
```
"Award-winning cinematography"
"Festival-quality production values"
"Commercial-grade professional"
"Broadcast-ready technical standards"
"Archival-quality preservation"
"Museum-exhibition standard"
"Gallery-level art photography"
```

**Example:**
```
Style: :cyberpunk aesthetic with brutalist architecture influences.
Unreal Engine 5 quality lighting and materials, ray-traced reflections.
1980s-inspired neon color palette with modern execution.
Award-winning cinematography, festival-quality composition.

Referenced aesthetics: Blade Runner-esque urban density
(described not named), Ghost in the Shell visual philosophy
(tech integration, not copying specific shots), akira-style
motion blur and speed lines (technique not IP).

Era: Neo-noir 2040s with 1980s retrofuturism, practical neon
sources, volumetric fog, reflective wet streets, vertical
urban architecture.
```

### Layer 12: NEGATIVE CONSTRAINTS

**Purpose:** Explicitly exclude unwanted artifacts, styles, and technical issues.

**Master Negative Prompt Template:**
```
AVOID: morphing objects, teleporting, floating physics,
impossible anatomy, extra fingers/limbs, distorted faces,
melting features, inconsistent lighting, random lens flares,
text/logos, watermarks, digital noise, compression artifacts,
color banding, AI aesthetic, plastic skin, waxy textures,
Dutch angles (unless specified), abrupt cuts, scale inconsistency,
flickering, color shifts, motion blur (unless specified)
```

**Category-Specific Negatives:**

**Physics/Motion:**
```
Exclude: objects passing through each other, gravity defying,
sudden appearance/disappearance, weightless motion,
inconsistent momentum, unnatural acceleration, impossible bends,
joints bending wrong direction
```

**Human Anatomy:**
```
Exclude: extra fingers (more than 5), missing fingers,
merged fingers, distorted hands, elongated limbs,
morphing facial features, inconsistent eye spacing,
unnatural neck angles, impossible body twists,
limb thickness inconsistency
```

**Visual Quality:**
```
Exclude: out-of-focus artifacts, blurry backgrounds (unless specified),
pixelation, low resolution feel, JPEG artifacts, moiré patterns,
chromatic aberration (unless specified), posterization, banding
```

**Lighting:**
```
Exclude: inconsistent light direction between shots,
unmotivated light sources, exposure flickering,
random shadows, physically impossible reflections,
light sources with no visible origin
```

**Style:**
```
Exclude: oversaturated colors (unless specified),
Instagram filter look, HDR overprocessing, stock photo aesthetic,
generic AI art feel, "perfect" digital rendering,
overly symmetrical unless architectural
```

**Strategic Constraint Usage:**

**Do:**
- Be specific about what to avoid
- Pair negatives with positives
- Focus on top 8-10 key exclusions
- Match constraints to desired style

**Don't:**
- Over-constrain (confuses model)
- Use vague negatives ("bad quality")
- Contradict your positive prompt
- Include negatives that oppose style

**Example:**
```
AVOID in this generation:
- Morphing: Maintain rigid object integrity throughout
- Floating physics: All objects obey gravity, appropriate weight
- Extra limbs: Exactly 2 arms, 2 legs, 10 fingers total, human anatomy
- Lens flares: No unmotivated flares (practical sources only)
- Text: No readable text, signage, logos anywhere in frame
- Digital noise: Use film grain only, no compression artifacts
- AI aesthetic: Avoid plasticky skin, over-smooth surfaces
- Inconsistent lighting: Key light stays camera-left throughout
- Motion blur: Sharp except during intentional movement

Positive opposites emphasized:
- Rigid carbon fiber maintains shape
- Objects have appropriate mass and weight
- Natural human proportions and movement
- Motivated practicals only (visible CRT glow, emergency lights)
- Clean surfaces without text
- Organic 35mm film grain at 20%
- Realistic skin texture with pores and imperfections
- Consistent lighting ratio 8:1 throughout
- Sharp focus on subject, natural motion blur on fast movements only
```

---

### BEATMAP + AUDIO DIRECTIVE

**Beatmap Notation:**
```
H0.00 | B2.00 | B4.00 | B6.00 | P8.00 | E10.00

H = Hook/Opening
B = Beat (action point)
P = Peak (climax)
E = End (resolution)
```

**Audio Directive Format:**
```
AUDIO:
Dialogue: "[Exact words]" (delivery style) at [timestamp]
Ambient: [Background sounds] constant/varying
SFX: [Specific sound] at [timestamp], [characteristics]
Music: [Style/mood] [intensity] [when it changes]
```

**Complete Example:**
```
Beatmap: H0.00 | B2.00 | B4.00 | B6.00 | P8.00 | E10.00

H0.00: Static establish, ambient only
B2.00: First action, SFX trigger
B4.00: Emotional shift, ambient change
B6.00: Dialogue begins
P8.00: Peak intensity, all layers active
E10.00: Resolution hold, ambient fade

AUDIO:
Dialogue: "This changes everything." (whispered, urgent) at 6.5s
Ambient: Low frequency hum (50Hz) constant throughout, fluorescent buzz
         layered at 20% volume, distant traffic ambience
SFX: Paper rustle at 2.0s (crisp, multiple sheets), keyboard typing at 3.5s,
     chair creak at 8.0s (wood, stressed)
Music: Subtle tension drone, building from 0-8s, peaks at 8s then sustains
```

---

## COMPLETE GODMODE EXAMPLE

Here's a full 12-layer prompt for reference:

**Prompt: "The Signal Hijack"**

```
LAYER 1 - REALISM ANCHOR:
Photorealistic, _DSC09421.ARW, shot on ARRI Alexa 65, 4K DCI resolution

LAYER 2 - SUBJECT & ACTION:
A weathered broadcast journalist, late 50s, salt-and-pepper hair,
rumpled white shirt with loosened tie, sits at cluttered 1980s news desk.
At 2s, shuffles stack of papers nervously, hands visibly trembling.
At 4s, stops, looks directly into camera with barely contained urgency.
At 6s, begins speaking, jaw muscles tensing. At 8s, glances off-camera
anxiously, as if hearing something. At 10s, returns gaze to camera,
holds intense eye contact, unblinking.

LAYER 3 - ENVIRONMENT:
Abandoned broadcast studio circa 1987. Water-stained acoustic ceiling tiles,
emergency exit signs casting red glow. Dust particles float through shafts
of emergency lighting. Multiple CRT monitors display static and test patterns,
casting irregular blue-green glow. XLR cables snake across concrete floor.
Rain visible through high cracked window, city lights bokeh in background.
Cold 4800K ambient mixed with warm 3200K monitor glow.

LAYER 4 - CAMERA SYSTEM:
ARRI Alexa 65, 4K DCI (4096×2160), 24fps, 180-degree shutter, ISO 800

LAYER 5 - LENS SPECIFICATIONS:
Cooke S4/i 50mm T2.0, medium close-up framing, gentle falloff,
warm Cooke character, shallow depth of field isolating subject
from cluttered background, subtle vignette

LAYER 6 - LIGHTING DESIGN:
Key light: Emergency lighting overhead, 4800K, hard quality, camera-left 45°
Fill light: CRT monitor glow, 7500K blue-green, 25% intensity, camera-right
Practical: Red emergency exit sign, background accent
Back light: Window ambient, 5000K, 50% intensity, creates subtle rim
Overall contrast ratio: 8:1 (dramatic but dimensional)

LAYER 7 - COLOR SCIENCE:
Palette:
Primary: #1a1a2e (deep blue-black) shadows and background
Secondary: #0f3460 (navy blue) mid-tones
Accent 1: #00d4ff (ice blue) CRT glow, highlights
Accent 2: #ff2a6d (hot pink/red) emergency lights, danger
Blacks: slightly crushed for depth
Whites: preserved in CRT highlights
Overall saturation: 90% (slightly muted, realistic)
Grade: Teal-and-orange bias with blue push, crushed blacks,
slight green cast in shadows for vintage broadcast feel.
Film grain: Kodak Vision3 500T character, 20% opacity.
Vignette: 15% darkening at frame edges.

LAYER 8 - MOTION CHOREOGRAPHY:
Camera: Slow push-in from medium to close-up, 1.0 ft/s over 8 seconds,
smooth gimbal stabilization, maintains eye level, begins 5 feet from subject,
ends at 2.5 feet for intimate final framing.

Subject: Seated position throughout. Micro-movements: breathing visible,
small head adjustments. At 2s, paper shuffle with hand tremor.
At 4-5.5s, slow head turn toward camera (20-degree rotation).
At 6s, speaking with minimal jaw movement. At 8s, quick glance
off-camera (30-degree snap), returns at 8.5s. Final stillness with
unblinking intensity.

Coordination: Camera push motivates viewer engagement. Arrives at
close-up exactly as subject completes emotional arc and locks eyes.

LAYER 9 - TEXTURE & DETAIL:
Skin: Visible pores, subsurface scattering, stubble texture, forehead
      shine, age-appropriate wrinkles, worry lines pronounced
Metal: CRT bezels with scratched plastic, dust accumulation in vents
Paper: Yellowed documents with fiber texture, creased edges
Fabric: Cotton shirt with visible weave, natural wrinkles, slight discoloration
Environment: Dust motes clearly visible in light shafts, cobweb in corner,
             water stains with organic patterns, cable insulation cracking
Film grain: 35mm aesthetic, 20% Kodak Vision3 500T texture, organic not digital

LAYER 10 - TEMPORAL CONTROL:
Duration: 10 seconds, 24fps, 180° shutter

Beatmap: H0.00 | B2.00 | B4.00 | B6.00 | P8.00 | E10.00

Timing:
H0.00: Static establish, subject visible but not yet engaging
B2.00: Paper shuffle begins, continues through 3.5s
B4.00: Head turn starts, slow rotation over 1.5s to camera
B6.00: Speaking begins at 6.5s: "This is unprecedented."
P8.00: Intensity peak, lean forward slightly, glance off-camera
E10.00: Final hold, unblinking eye contact, 1.5s static

LAYER 11 - STYLE ANCHORS:
Style: 1980s broadcast news aesthetic, analog horror influences,
:horrorcore atmosphere, abandoned institutional spaces.
Cinematic quality, festival-level production values.
Film noir lighting principles applied to broadcast setting.
Documentary realism meets psychological tension.
Award-winning cinematography with intentional period accuracy.

LAYER 12 - NEGATIVE CONSTRAINTS:
AVOID: morphing facial features, extra fingers, plastic skin texture,
lens flares (except motivated CRT glare), text/logos visible,
modern technology (smartphones, flat screens), clean/pristine environment,
bright cheerful lighting, oversaturation, AI aesthetic smoothness,
motion blur except natural camera movement, inconsistent lighting direction,
Dutch angles, abrupt movements, floating objects, impossible physics

POSITIVE REINFORCEMENT: maintain consistent facial structure,
natural human proportions, realistic skin texture with imperfections,
motivated light sources only (emergency + CRT), period-appropriate
technology, lived-in wear and damage, moody dramatic lighting,
muted realistic color, organic film grain, intentional motion blur
only during camera push, 8:1 lighting ratio maintained, level framing,
smooth deliberate movements, objects obey gravity, realistic physics

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════

BEATMAP: H0.00 | B2.00 | B4.00 | B6.00 | P8.00 | E10.00

AUDIO DIRECTIVE:
Dialogue: "This is unprecedented." (measured, serious, slightly trembling)
          spoken at 6.5-8.0s, clear enunciation
Ambient: Low 60Hz electrical hum constant, fluorescent buzz at 15% volume,
         distant rain patter through window, building ambience
SFX: Paper rustle at 2.0-3.5s (multiple sheets, nervous handling),
     CRT static crackle subtle background, chair creak at 8.0s (wood, stressed),
     breathing audible in quiet moments
Music: None - pure diegetic sound only
```

This complete example demonstrates maximum control across all 12 layers, resulting in a specific, reproducible, high-quality output.
